        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. sodium insertion for hard carbon is examd. in a cyclic alkylene carbonate-based soln. contg. sodium perchlorate (NaClO4) or sodium hexafluorophosphate (NaPF6) salt with fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) additive to study electrolyte dependency for Na-ion batteries.  NaPF6-based electrolytes provided superior reversibility and cyclability of sodium insertion into hard carbon compared to NaClO4-based ones.  The FEC-derived passivation film improves the capacity retention because of better passivation with a thinner surface layer, which is revealed by hard and soft XPS (PES).  Using both the NaPF6 salt and FEC additive results in a synergetic effect on passivation for the hard-carbon electrode, leading to enhanced cycle performance.  Hard-carbon electrodes with poly (vinylede difluoride) binder in propylene carbonate-based electrolytes contg. NaPF6 and FEC demonstrates the excellent capacity retention with reversible capacity of ca. 250 mAh g-1.  The difference in capacity retention for the electrolytes is expected to originate from a consequence of the difference in the surface interphase layer formed on the hard-carbon electrodes.  Surface analyses with PES and time-of-flight secondary ion mass spectroscopy revealed differences in surface and passivation chem., which depends on the salts, solvents, and FEC additive used for the hard-carbon neg. electrodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref22" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.6b03403"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kumar, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Detsi, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Abraham, D. P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shenoy, V.                 10.1021/acs.chemmater.6b03403</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D28%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D8930-8941%26journal%3DChem.%2BMater.%26author%3DH.%2BKumar%26author%3DE.%2BDetsi%26author%3DD.%2BP.%2BAbraham%26author%3DV.%2BB.%2BShenoy%26title%3DFundamental%2BMechanisms%2Bof%2BSolvent%2BDecomposition%2BInvolved%2Bin%2BSolid%2BElectrolyte%2BInterphase%2BFormation%2Bin%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.chemmater.6b03403&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c20542&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.chemmater.6b03403&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fundamental Mechanisms of Solvent Decomposition Involved in Solid-Electrolyte Interphase Formation in Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kumar, Hemant; Detsi, Eric; Abraham, Daniel P.; Shenoy, Vivek B.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">28</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">24</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8930-8941</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prolonged decompn. of electrolytes forming a thick and unstable solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) continues to be a major bottleneck in designing sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  We have carried out quantum chem. simulations to investigate the fundamental mechanisms of redn.-induced decompn. of electrolyte solvents in the vicinity of a sodium ion.  Kinetics and thermodn. of several reaction pathways for one- and two-electron redn. of ethylene carbonate (EC) have been examd.  Our calcns. indicate that the high redn. potential and low barrier for the ring opening of EC is the main cause for the continuous growth of SEI obsd. in SIBs.  The impact of two well-known electrolyte additives, vinyl carbonate (VC) and fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC), on SEI compn. was evaluated by studying decompn. pathways of (1) VC and FEC mols. in the bulk EC solvent and (2) an EC mol. in a supermol. cluster comprising an EC and the additive mol.  The additive mols. have significantly low barriers for decompn. and therefore decomp. first.  Addnl., the presence of an additive mol. was also shown to increase the barrier for decompn. of EC.  Another observation suggests that the preferred redn. state of an EC mol. changes when it forms a dimer with additive mols., and these redn. states have different decompn. pathways which leads to formation of different SEI compds.  On the basis of these observations, we predict that not only do the additive mols. protect solvent mols. from reductive decompn. but also they can promote alternate pathways for the decompn., leading to qual. different and potentially stable SEI products.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref23" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1002/cssc.201601356"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gai, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Density Functional Theory Research into the Reduction Mechanism for the Solvent/Additive in a Sodium Ion Battery</span>. <i>ChemSusChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">786</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">796</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/cssc.201601356</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D786-796%26journal%3DChemSusChem%26author%3DQ.%2BLiu%26author%3DD.%2BMu%26author%3DB.%2BWu%26author%3DL.%2BWang%26author%3DL.%2BGai%26author%3DF.%2BWu%26title%3DDensity%2BFunctional%2BTheory%2BResearch%2Binto%2Bthe%2BReduction%2BMechanism%2Bfor%2Bthe%2BSolvent%252FAdditive%2Bin%2Ba%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBattery%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fcssc.201601356&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.0c20542&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fcssc.201601356&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Density Functional Theory Research into the Reduction Mechanism for the Solvent/Additive in a Sodium-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Qi; Mu, Daobin; Wu, Borong; Wang, Lei; Gai, Liang; Wu, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemSusChem</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">786-796</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHEMIZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1864-5631</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The solid-electrolyte interface (SEI) film in a sodium-ion battery is closely related to capacity fading and cycling stability of the battery.  However, there are few studies on the SEI film of sodium-ion batteries and the mechanism of SEI film formation is unclear.  The mechanism for the redn. of ethylene carbonate (EC), propylene carbonate (PC), vinylene carbonate (VC), ethylene sulfite (ES), 1,3-propylene sulfite (PS), and fluorinated ethylene carbonate (FEC) is studied by DFT.  The reaction activation energies, Gibbs free energies, enthalpies, and structures of the transition states are calcd.  It is indicated that VC, ES, and PS additives in the electrolyte are all easier to form org. components in the anode SEI film by one-electron redn.  The priority of one-electron redn. to produce org. SEI components is in the order of VC&gt;PC&gt;EC; two-electron redn. to produce the inorg. Na2CO3 component is different and follows the order of EC&gt;PC&gt;VC.  Two-electron redn. for sulfites ES and PS to form inorg. Na2SO3 is harder than that of carbonate ester redn.  It is also suggested that the one- and two-electron reductive decompn. pathway for FEC is more feasible to produce inorg. NaF components.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="9318807a4b8e54b8-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

Hard C (HC) is the state-of-the-art anode material for Na-ion batteries due to its excellent overall performance, wide availability, and relatively low cost.  Recently, tremendous effort has been invested to elucidate the sodium storage mechanism in HC, and to explore synthetic approaches that can enhance the performance and lower the cost.  However, disagreements remain in the field, particularly on the fundamental questions of ion transfer and storage and the ideal HC structure for high performance.  This paper provides an anal. and summary of the theor. limitations of HC, discrepancies in the storage mechanism, and methods to improve the performance.  Future research on developing ideal structured HCs, advanced electrolytes, and optimized electrolyte-electrode interphases are proposed on the basis of recent progress.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.mattod.2018.12.040"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hasa, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Saurel, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vaalma, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Buchholz, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bresser, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Passerini, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hard Carbons for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Structure, Analysis, Sustainability, and Electrochemistry</span>. <i>Mater.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Hard carbons are extensively studied for application as anode materials in sodium-ion batteries, but only recently a great interest has been focused toward the understanding of the sodium storage mechanism and the comprehension of the structure-function correlation.  Although several interesting mechanisms have been proposed, a general mechanism explaining the obsd. electrochem. processes is still missing, which is essentially originating from the remaining uncertainty on the complex hard carbons structure.  The achievement of an in-depth understanding of the processes occurring upon sodiation, however, is of great importance for a rational design of optimized anode materials.In this review, we aim at providing a comprehensive overview of the up-to-date known structural models of hard carbons and their correlation with the proposed models for the sodium-ion storage mechanisms.  In this regard, a particular focus is set on the most powerful anal. tools to study the structure of hard carbons (upon de-/sodiation) and a crit. discussion on how to interpret and perform such anal.  Targeting the eventual commercialization of hard carbon anodes for sodium-ion batteries - after having established a fundamental understanding - we close this review with a careful evaluation of potential strategies to ensure a high degree of sustainability, since this is undoubtedly a crucial parameter to take into account for the future large-scale prodn. of hard carbons.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1016/j.elecom.2013.10.008"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Singh, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Acebedo, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Casas-Cabanas, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shanmukaraj, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Armand, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rojo, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Approach to Overcome First Cycle Irreversible Capacity in P<sub>2</sub>-Na<sub>2/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/2</sub>Mn<sub>1/2</sub>O<sub>2</sub></span>. <i>Electrochem.                 10.1016/j.elecom.2013.10.008</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An approach to overcome first cycle irreversible capacity in P2-Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Singh, Gurpreet; Acebedo, Begona; Cabanas, Montse Casas; Shanmukaraj, Devaraj; Armand, Michel; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochemistry Communications</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The Earth-abundant high capacity Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2 sodium-ion battery cathode material has been synthesized by conventional solid state synthesis.  X-ray diffraction measurement shows the formation of the single phase Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2.  SEM shows particle size in the micron range having hexagonal morphol. with high aspect ratio.  To circumvent the first cycle irreversible capacity loss in Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2, NaN3 has been used as a source of extra Na ions added to the cathode mix.  While pristine P2 type Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2 exhibits an irreversible capacity of 59 mAh/g, it reduces to 27 mAh/g after adding 5 wt.% NaN3 with concomitant nitrogen evolution in the half cell configuration. We have carried out quantum chem. simulations to investigate the fundamental mechanisms of redn.-induced decompn. of electrolyte solvents in the vicinity of a sodium ion.  Kinetics and thermodn. of several reaction pathways for one- and two-electron redn. of ethylene carbonate (EC) have been examd.  Our calcns. indicate that the high redn. potential and low barrier for the ring opening of EC is the main cause for the continuous growth of SEI obsd. in SIBs.  The impact of two well-known electrolyte additives, vinyl carbonate (VC) and fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC), on SEI compn. was evaluated by studying decompn. pathways of (1) VC and FEC mols. in the bulk EC solvent and (2) an EC mol. in a supermol. cluster comprising an EC and the additive mol.  The additive mols. have significantly low barriers for decompn. and therefore decomp. first.  Addnl., the presence of an additive mol. was also shown to increase the barrier for decompn. of EC.  Another observation suggests that the preferred redn. state of an EC mol. changes when it forms a dimer with additive mols., and these redn. states have different decompn. pathways which leads to formation of different SEI compds.  On the basis of these observations, we predict that not only do the additive mols. protect solvent mols. from reductive decompn. but also they can promote alternate pathways for the decompn., leading to qual. different and potentially stable SEI products.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref23" class="rightTabRefNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit23" data-doi="10.1002/cssc.201601356"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gai, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Density Functional Theory Research into the Reduction Mechanism for the Solvent/Additive in a Sodium Ion Battery</span>. <i>ChemSusChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">786</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">796</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/cssc.201601356</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Density Functional Theory Research into the Reduction Mechanism for the Solvent/Additive in a Sodium-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Qi; Mu, Daobin; Wu, Borong; Wang, Lei; Gai, Liang; Wu, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemSusChem</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">786-796</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHEMIZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1864-5631</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The solid-electrolyte interface (SEI) film in a sodium-ion battery is closely related to capacity fading and cycling stability of the battery.  However, there are few studies on the SEI film of sodium-ion batteries and the mechanism of SEI film formation is unclear.  The mechanism for the redn. of ethylene carbonate (EC), propylene carbonate (PC), vinylene carbonate (VC), ethylene sulfite (ES), 1,3-propylene sulfite (PS), and fluorinated ethylene carbonate (FEC) is studied by DFT.  The reaction activation energies, Gibbs free energies, enthalpies, and structures of the transition states are calcd.  It is indicated that VC, ES, and PS additives in the electrolyte are all easier to form org. components in the anode SEI film by one-electron redn.  The priority of one-electron redn. to produce org. SEI components is in the order of VC&gt;PC&gt;EC; two-electron redn. to produce the inorg. Na2CO3 component is different and follows the order of EC&gt;PC&gt;VC.  Two-electron redn. for sulfites ES and PS to form inorg. Na2SO3 is harder than that of carbonate ester redn.  It is also suggested that the one- and two-electron reductive decompn. pathway for FEC is more feasible to produce inorg. NaF components.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-5"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i13">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.0c20542?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.0c20542</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Comparison of charge profiles of sacrificial sodium salt/carbon mixture with C65 and KJ600 carbon (Figure S1); synthesis procedure and galvanostatic cycling and coulombic efficiency of HC in half-cell configuration with sodium metal anode (Figure S2); Rietveld refinement of pristine P2–Na<sub>2/3</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>Fe<sub>0.1</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> powder XRD pattern (Figure S3); SEM micrographs of pristine P2–Na<sub>2/3</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>Fe<sub>0.1</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> at different magnifications (Figure S4); X-ray diffractogram of Na<sub>2</sub>C<sub>3</sub>O<sub>5</sub> after different heat treatments (Figure S5); SEM micrographs of Na<sub>2</sub>C<sub>3</sub>O<sub>5</sub> salt after composite mixing with carbon (Figure S6); SEM micrographs of P2–Na<sub>2/3</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>Fe<sub>0.1</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> mixed with Na<sub>2</sub>C<sub>3</sub>O<sub>5</sub> before cycling and after the first cycle (Figure S7); comparison of the C 1s photoelectron spectra of P2–Na<sub>2/3</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>Fe<sub>0.1</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> from ref  <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref12" aria-label="reference 12">(12)</a> and P2–Na<sub>2/3</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>Fe<sub>0.1</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> + Na<sub>2</sub>C<sub>3</sub>O<sub>5</sub>—this work—after 10 cycles (Figure S8); and comparison of the O 1s photoelectron spectra of P2–Na<sub>2/3</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>Fe<sub>0.1</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> from ref  <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref12" aria-label="reference 12">(12)</a> and P2–Na<sub>2/3</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>Fe<sub>0.1</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> + Na<sub>2</sub>C<sub>3</sub>O<sub>5</sub>—this work (Figure S9) (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.0c20542/suppl_file/am0c20542_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.0c20542/suppl_file/am0c20542_si_001.pdf">am0c20542_si_001.pdf (727.88 kb)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();

	});

		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

<script nonce="9318807a4b8e54b8-SJC">
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {
    const modalContainer = document.querySelector('.my-main-container');

    // Function to show the modal
    function showModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'flex';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'block';
    }

    // Function to hide the modal when the close button is clicked
    function hideModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'none';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'none';
    }

    // Hide the modal initially
    hideModal();

    // Function to handle clicks outside the modal
    function handleClickOutside(event) {
        // const modalContainer = document.querySelector(".my-main-container");
        // Check if the click target is not a child of the modal container
        if (!modalContainer.contains(event.target)) {
            hideModal();
        }
    }

    // Add a click event listener to the close button
    document
        .querySelector('.close-button')
        .addEventListener('click', hideModal);

    // Add a click event listener to the document to handle clicks outside the modal
    document.addEventListener('click', handleClickOutside);

    const screenHeight = window.innerHeight;
    function updateModalPosition() {
        const scrollY = window.scrollY;
        // console.log("scrollY= " + scrollY);
        // modalContainer.style.top = `${50 + scrollY}px`;
        modalContainer.style.top = `${scrollY + screenHeight / 2}px`;
        // console.log("new top= " + modalContainer.style.top);
    }

    // Update the modal position when the user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', updateModalPosition);

    // Initialize the modal position
    updateModalPosition();

    //---Cookie---
    // Function to set the cookie with a given name, value, and expiration time in days
    function setCookie(name, value, days) {
        var expires = '';
        if (days) {
            var date = new Date();
            date.setTime(date.getTime() + days * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);
            expires = '; expires=' + date.toUTCString();
            console.log(expires + 'this is expires dateUTC');
        }
        document.cookie = name + '=' + (value || '') + expires + '; path=/';
        // console.log("document.cookie is: " + document.cookie);
    }

    if (!document.cookie.includes('modalAd')) {
        // Show Modal
        showModal();

        // Set the cookie with the name "modalAd", value "true", and expiration of 3 day
        setCookie('modalAd', 'true', 3);
    } else {
        hideModal();
    }
});

</script>

<script nonce="9318807a4b8e54b8-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

      function init() {

      //Show the message
      function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();
      }

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
      }

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

    $(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
  </script>
</p>
-->

                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="9318807a4b8e54b8-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>
